COMMENT     This version of genes, transcripts, and proteins was created in
            April 2002 from the whole-genome mapping of transcript and protein
            sequences on the Celera human genome assembly
            (http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/genome/guide/human/release_notes.html)
            by Celera Chromosome Team, Content Systems and Informatics
            Research. The data sets used by this annotation process were
            collected in 2001 and include RefSeq (NM_) sequences, manually
            annotated transcripts from previous Celera assemblies, GenBank mRNA
            and dbEST sequences, Celera internal EST and full-insert sequences
            of cDNA clones (unpublished), mammalian SwissProt sequences, NRAA
            sequences, and International Protein Index (IPI) sequences (all
            human unless noted otherwise).  The CDS of each transcript was
            computationally defined by either the longest ATG-to-Stop or the
            longest open reading frame. All CDSs corresponding to the longest
            open reading frames with no starting ATG were flagged as partial.
            In addition, some of the genes were manually curated between 2002
            and 2005. Coverage analysis of splice junction donor/acceptor pairs
            and single-exon transcripts was done by Applied Biosystems in
            August 2006, based on Dec 2005 versions of human cDNA (RefSeq,
            Genbank mRNA and dbEST, Celera internal EST and full insert
            sequences) and human SwissProt sequences.
            This is the November 2001 combined whole genome shotgun assembly
            applied to the 27 million reads of Celera's whole genome shotgun
            data and 16 million  reads of shredded GenBank data from other
            human genome projects (Nature 2001. 409:860-921). It relied on
            Celera's paired reads and BAC end reads from TIGR for long range
            order and orientation. Its scaffolds were mapped to chromosomes
            using STS maps. For more detailed information about whole genome
            sequencing and Celera's assembly process, please refer to Venter,
            J.C. et al. Science 2001. 291:1304-1351.
